--- Commit Message ---
LU-11912 ofd: reduce LUSTRE_DATA_SEQ_MAX_WIDTH

Reduce LUSTRE_DATA_SEQ_MAX_WIDTH from ~4B to ~32M
to limit the number of objects under /O/[seq]/d[0..31]
dir on OSTs.
This makes the directories stay optimial for ldiskfs,
to avoid going into the largedir/3-level htree territory.

Remove the hard-coded LUSTRE_DATA_SEQ_MAX_WIDTH checks
in ofd, make them check the seq->lcs_width which is
a tunable set to LUSTRE_DATA_SEQ_MAX_WIDTH by default,
allow the value up to IDIF_MAX_OID if a larger seq width
is needed.

Use the odbo->o_size in the OST_CREATE rpc reply on ofd,
to update osp with the current seq width setting.
osp then uses this seq width to determine when to rollover
to a new seq.

The seq will rollover when the seq width is exhausted,
the default is LUSTRE_DATA_SEQ_MAX_WIDTH.
For seq >= FID_SEQ_NORMAL objects, the upper limit of
seq width is OBIF_MAX_OID,
For IDIF/MDT0 objects, the upper limit is IDIF_MAX_OID.
The seq FID_SEQ_OST_MDT0 will change to a normal seq after the
rollover.

Fix osp_precreate_reserve when the last precreated is the end
of the seq and the osp_objs_precreated can not host all
the requested objects, the mdt thread would stuck:
it wakes up osp precreate thread in a loop for progress,
but osp thread will not try to do anything until the seq
is used up. This can be seen easier when seq->lcs_width is
set to a low number and try to create an overstripe with stripe
number bigger than seq->lcs_width.

Fix the precreate thread spinning when the precreate pool
is at the end of the seq, and is nearly empty.

Change the seq->lcs_width to 16384 for all tests in
test-framework.sh, except a few slow tests to avoid timeouts,
and some overstriping tests creating LOV_MAX_STRIPE_COUNT to
avoid overstriping creating less objects than expected,
when precreate pool is at the end of the seq, and there are
not enough objects.

Fix the problem where seq could still change after
replay_barrier. To achieve this, introduce new fail_loc
OBD_FAIL_OSP_FORCE_NEW_SEQ and force_new_seq/force_new_seq_all
to drain the objects in the precreate pool then rollover to a
new seq. This applies to a bunch of test suites heavily using
replay_barrier.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2020-04-30 10:00:45.000000000) ---
Patch Set 1: Code-Review-1

(7 comments)

This definitely needs a test case, and some way to verify that SEQ rollover is working properly.  Otherwise, we may run into bugs like LU-9547 that are not hit during normal regression testing (I don't think we create 32M objects on an OST in a regular test run.

The best way to test this code (and to make the code more usable) is to use a tunable parameter to be able to change the maximum SEQ width that is being used by the MDS.  Please see my lengthy comment/description in LU-11912 of what appears to be missing to be able to tune the SEQ width at runtime.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2021-11-25 22:28:38.000000000) ---
Patch Set 6:

(12 comments)

> how do we tell the test system to set seq width to 4096 on all the OSTs?
 > I looked up Test-Parameters wiki and seems it doesn't do this sort of things?

I was thinking of doing this permanently for all tests by changing test-framework.sh, not just for this patch with Test-Parameters.  

Something like the following right at the end of mount_facet() whenever an MDT is mounted:

        [[ $facet =~ mds ]] &&
                do_nodes $(comma_list $(osts_nodes)) "$LCTL set_param -P seq.cli-cli-$FSNAME-OST*-osc-*.width=4096"

though there is a potential ordering issue since (AFAIK) these seq.cli-cli-*.width entries are created when the MDT connects to the OST.  That means if the OSTs are mounted after the MDTs they would not exist at MDT mount time, and similarly if OSTs are mounted before MDTs t then the MDS connections would not be set up correctly yet.  This will also be an issue if some customer wants to change this parameter, so it would be good to have a proper solution.

One opition is having an obdfilter.*.seq_width parameter that is copied when each MDT connects?  However, if it is changed after the MDS connects, it wouldn't be updated until the next connection.  Not great, but unlikely to be a significant problem for production use.   

That would change the test-framework.sh::mount_facet() code to:

        [[ $facet =~ ost ]] &&
                do_facet $facet "$LCTL set_param obdfilter.*.seq_width=4096

One other issue I realized when thinking about how the different IDIF_MAX_SEQ and OBIF_MAX_SEQ values are handled, is that using IDIF SEQ values with a smaller seq_width will NOT actually change MDT0000 object creation to a new O/* directory tree when f_seq is incremented.  That is because 2^16 IDIF f_seq values from MDT0000 *all* map to the same O/0/d* directory tree, so limiting the values to seq_width will only cause a gap (4B - seq_width) in the OID number, but continue to be created in the same O/0 directory tree until MDT0000 creates 2^16 * 32M = 2T objects (or 2^16 * 4096 = 256M objects during testing).

In order to get MDT0000 to properly create OST objects in different O/<seq>/d* directories, it should stop using the IDIF sequence right from the beginning, so I think it makes sense to implement LU-14692 first and base this patch on top of that one.

It looks like this failure is caused by the patch:

 osp_fid_diff()) ASSERTION( fid_seq(fid1) == fid_seq(fid2) ) failed:
           fid1:[0x380000404:0x2:0x0], fid2:[0x380000403:0x1000:0x0]

the FID sequence has _just_ wrapped around in this case.  Does it make sense to change osp_fid_diff() to take the different SEQ numbers into account, by returning "1" for the difference if there is a new sequence number?

Patch Set 8:

> > Failed enforced test review-dne-zfs-part-6 on CentOS 8.3/x86_64
 > > uploaded by Onyx Autotest from onyx-70vm6: https://testing.whamcloud.com/test_sessions/edec2253-9bb0-48c7-ba0b-49cb98a55e3f
 > > ran 6 tests.  1 tests failed: replay-single.
 > > %% THIS TEST SESSION CRASHED %%
 > 
 > It looks like this failure is caused by the patch:
 > 
 > osp_fid_diff()) ASSERTION( fid_seq(fid1) == fid_seq(fid2) ) failed:
 > fid1:[0x380000404:0x2:0x0], fid2:[0x380000403:0x1000:0x0]
 > 
 > the FID sequence has _just_ wrapped around in this case.  Does it
 > make sense to change osp_fid_diff() to take the different SEQ
 > numbers into account, by returning "1" for the difference if there
 > is a new sequence number?

I've been looking into this, was able to reproduce and got kdump.
Looks like during replay, mdt had no idea we just got new seq before the replay, the smaller seq width makes the seq change more frequent
and made the issue easier to show.

I've kept the LASSERT in osp_fid_diff() but returns 1 if we are just starting with the new seq.

 > With MAX_WIDTH=4096 this means 128 entries per subdirectory, and
 > sync creates as the sequence is exhausted, which may hurt
 > performance.  This test with 7 OSTs would fill the sequence every
 > 28k creates, so it would have wrapped 3x.  It would be good to see
 > if there is something causing this to be *so* slow,  make sense to
 > temporarily increase the seq_width for this test (and others that
 > create tens of thousands of files) to avoid the timeout?

I've tried many times but unfortunately on my setup I could not see that level of create time,
I'm getting at least 200 to 300 op/s with 4096 seq_width.

There are quite a number of other tests creating many files as well,
instead of temporarily increase the seq_width for those tests, I've increased it to 16384, which will gives us reasonable number of seq updates and hopefully won't slow down the tests

> I guess the question remains - what happens if an overstriped file is created close to the end of the sequence on a real filesystem?

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2023-03-09 14:49:12.000000000) ---
Patch Set 25: Code-Review+1

> The file is still created, but with less stripes, up to the number of objects available in the precreate pool

I guess that's not so bad, since it is unlikely that all OSTs will be exactly at the end of their sequence at the same time, and with multiple OSTs there should still be a number of objects available. 

The other option would be to pre-check the number of objects available for each OST when overstriping a file and advance to the next sequence early, but I'm not sure if that is worthwhile or not, given the (AFAIK) low usage of overstriping in the field.

--- Message (Li Dongyang, 2023-03-15 14:17:31.000000000) ---
Patch Set 26:

(3 comments)

> Patch Set 26:
> 
> > Patch Set 26:
> > 
> > (6 comments)
> > 
> > I have the feeling that this recent test change is working around a real problem that will eventually be seen on the field. While setting reply_barrier isn't typical in the field, it seems possible that the same thing could happen with a SEQ rollover plus a badly-timed MDS crash. That is essentially what replay_barrier is simulating - a crash at just the wrong time.
> 
> If it is possible to get such panic in the field, we should think how to avoid it in advance. Dongyang, could you please explain in several words why did it fail and from which place osp_fid_diff was called(this should be seen from the crash dump)?

Andreas, my impression is we do need to make sure no seq changes during replay_barrier, and the crash is unlikely to happen on the field.
If the MDS crashed when rolling over the seq, it won't continue hand out the fids with new seq to clients, which could trigger the crash later in replay due to mismatch seq, like we saw earlier with replay_single test_70c.
The comment in replay_barrier also reads "make sure there will be no seq change" however that seems to be broken.

Sergey, we would get this crash in the field if we met exactly the conditions in replay_barrier,
which means when MDT updates the new seq it's going to use the storage reports write being done but it never hits the disk/silently drops the write. Then MDT continue with create rpc, telling the client FIDs with new seq.
After a restart/failover MDT reads the seq it was using and got the old one, then replay rpc happens, the client sending the FID with new seq and triggers the LASSERT.
The call chain is like this: osp_create()->osp_update_last_fid()->osp_fid_diff().

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2023-03-15 20:28:56.000000000) ---
Patch Set 26:

(1 comment)

Dongyang, I was thinking the reason this might happen in the field is right after SEQ update that the MDS allocates some objects with the new SEQ and returns those to clients, but doesn't commit the SEQ update to disk. However, I now recall that SEQ rollover *should* be totally synchronous (ie. no new object allocations until after SEQ update is committed safely), so it would normally only be hit with replay_barrier discarding sync writes and journal commits.  However, it _might_ also be hit if the journal commit was lost before it was checkpointed to the filesystem (corrupt journal/e2fsck or write cache loss in the controller).

Also, does a risk exist if *old* objects come in during replay with the old SEQ and the FID difference is suddenly huge?  It might still make sense to relax/fix the LASSERT() so that it can handle/ignore small differences in SEQ numbers?

Have you checked the test logs to see that SEQ rollovers are happening during normal testing?  I'm wondering if the "problem" subtests that are using a lot of objects and causing rollover are being hidden by forcing a new SEQ or expanding the width?

--- Message (Li Dongyang, 2023-03-16 00:44:05.000000000) ---
Patch Set 26:

(1 comment)

> Patch Set 26:
> 
> (1 comment)
> 
> Dongyang, I was thinking the reason this might happen in the field is right after SEQ update that the MDS allocates some objects with the new SEQ and returns those to clients, but doesn't commit the SEQ update to disk. However, I now recall that SEQ rollover *should* be totally synchronous (ie. no new object allocations until after SEQ update is committed safely), so it would normally only be hit with replay_barrier discarding sync writes and journal commits.  However, it _might_ also be hit if the journal commit was lost before it was checkpointed to the filesystem (corrupt journal/e2fsck or write cache loss in the controller).
> 
> Also, does a risk exist if *old* objects come in during replay with the old SEQ and the FID difference is suddenly huge?  It might still make sense to relax/fix the LASSERT() so that it can handle/ignore small differences in SEQ numbers?
> 
> Have you checked the test logs to see that SEQ rollovers are happening during normal testing?  I'm wondering if the "problem" subtests that are using a lot of objects and causing rollover are being hidden by forcing a new SEQ or expanding the width?

Yes the SEQ rollover is synchronous, no new FID allocation until it's committed. If we are looking at losing journal commit or write cache loss in controller we are in a deeper trouble already.

When the SEQ rollover to a new one, it's not always the immediate next value, the SEQ client got a range and when the range is used up, a new range is allocated for it. So I don't think we can relax the LASSERT to handle/ignore the small differences.

Now the risk of seeing old SEQ during replay, I think there should be some ordering in place,
when the SEQ rollover is committed, the transactions before it should be committed first so clients will free the RPCs using the old SEQ, as replay is not needed for them.
Plus the SEQ roller commit being synchronous is the other half, so clients won't have the replay RPC with new SEQ but after crash server only sees the old.

So sounds like the SEQ rollover commit should just be like the journal commit log with block barrier in place? I'm not sure if this ordering is already in place. Andreas do you know if we already have this or not? I will also investigate.

Yes during the test runs the SEQ rollover can happen a lot, mostly in sanity. and it's a bit random(which is good) when we have different number of OSTs.

--- Message (Sergey Cheremencev, 2023-03-16 11:16:39.000000000) ---
Patch Set 27: Code-Review+1

> Patch Set 26:
> 
> (3 comments)
> 
> > Patch Set 26:
> > 
> > > Patch Set 26:
> > > 
> > > (6 comments)
> > > 
> > > I have the feeling that this recent test change is working around a real problem that will eventually be seen on the field. While setting reply_barrier isn't typical in the field, it seems possible that the same thing could happen with a SEQ rollover plus a badly-timed MDS crash. That is essentially what replay_barrier is simulating - a crash at just the wrong time.
> > 
> > If it is possible to get such panic in the field, we should think how to avoid it in advance. Dongyang, could you please explain in several words why did it fail and from which place osp_fid_diff was called(this should be seen from the crash dump)?
> 
> Andreas, my impression is we do need to make sure no seq changes during replay_barrier, and the crash is unlikely to happen on the field.
> If the MDS crashed when rolling over the seq, it won't continue hand out the fids with new seq to clients, which could trigger the crash later in replay due to mismatch seq, like we saw earlier with replay_single test_70c.
> The comment in replay_barrier also reads "make sure there will be no seq change" however that seems to be broken.
> 
> Sergey, we would get this crash in the field if we met exactly the conditions in replay_barrier,
> which means when MDT updates the new seq it's going to use the storage reports write being done but it never hits the disk/silently drops the write. Then MDT continue with create rpc, telling the client FIDs with new seq.
> After a restart/failover MDT reads the seq it was using and got the old one, then replay rpc happens, the client sending the FID with new seq and triggers the LASSERT.
> The call chain is like this: osp_create()->osp_update_last_fid()->osp_fid_diff().

Ok, thank you. Just a thought. What if don't trigger a panic in a such case? We can change osp_fid_diff to print warning depending on extra input argument and return error into osp_update_last_fid->osp_create. On the other hand, this shouldn't happen too often and sometimes it is better to figure out why did we get such case.
